# Awesome AI Researchers [![Awesome](https://awesome.re/badge.svg)](https://awesome.re) [![License: CC0-1.0](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-CC0%201.0-lightgrey.svg)](LICENSE)

**Languages:** [![日本語](https://img.shields.io/badge/lang-%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E8%AA%9E-lightgrey)](README.md) [![English](https://img.shields.io/badge/lang-English-blue)](README.en.md)

> A cross-field curated list of **researchers whose work has had sustained impact across AI-related areas**, intended as a starting point for research surveys. It covers affiliations, current countries and origins broadly, spanning both academia and industry, from classic pioneers to active top researchers.

**Researchers: 1029** / 20 fields (last updated: 2026-06-05)

## Legend / Inclusion Criteria

Researchers are included when they satisfy one or more of the following criteria (with field-specific adjustments and exceptions):

- They publish **sustained, influential work** in top conferences or journals.
- They are prolific in major venues and/or have very high citation impact.
- They made **foundational contributions** to the field, including classics or breakthroughs.
- They received major awards such as Turing / Gödel / Nevanlinna / Test-of-Time awards or society fellowships.

Entries use the format `Name — affiliation (country; origin) — research topics; representative contributions 🏆 awards 📊 metrics`. Citation counts and h-index values are approximate.

> Detailed metadata, full research results and field/region statistics are in [docs/research-notes.md](docs/research-notes.md); the collection methodology is in [docs/best-practice.md](docs/best-practice.md) (Japanese).

## 🧠 Machine Learning (NeurIPS / ICML / ICLR / UAI / ACML)

- **[Aapo Hyvärinen](https://www.cs.helsinki.fi/u/ahyvarin/)** — University of Helsinki (Finland) — Independent component analysis, score matching, self-supervised learning theory; Independent component analysis (FastICA), score matching (basics of diffusion model), nonlinear ICA and identifiability theory 🏆高被引用研究者、IEEE論文多数 · 📊70,000+ citations / h-index 60+ (approx.)
- **[Aaron Courville](https://mila.quebec/en/directory/aaron-courville)** — Université de Montréal / Mila (Canada) — Representation learning, deep generative models, self-supervised learning, reinforcement learning; Co-author of deep generative models (GAN/conditional generation), theory and methods of representation learning, and standard deep learning textbook (Deep Learning). 🏆Canada CIFAR AI Chair · 📊~350,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Aditi Raghunathan](https://www.cs.cmu.edu/~aditirag/)** — Carnegie Mellon University (United States; origin: India) — Robustness, distribution shift, proof of adversarial robustness, reliability of the underlying model; He led the theoretical analysis of certified defenses of adversarial robustness, out-of-distribution generalization, and robustness-accuracy trade-offs. 🏆Arthur Samuel Best Thesis Award (Stanford), Google PhD Fellowship · 📊~22,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Albert Gu](https://goombalab.github.io/)** — Carnegie Mellon University / Cartesia AI (USA) — State space model, S4, Mamba, long series modeling; Leader of Structured State Space Models (S4) and Mamba (Selective SSM). Established a linear time series architecture to replace Transformer. 🏆COLM Outstanding Paper (Mamba), TIME100 AI · 📊approx. 15,000+
- **[Alexander J. Smola](https://alex.smola.org/)** — Boson AI / 元Amazon (United States; origin: Germany) — Kernel method, support vector machine, scalable learning, kernel average embedding; Kernel method/SVM theory (co-authored with Learning with Kernels), Hilbert space embedding of distributions, and building the foundation of large-scale machine learning systems. 🏆ACM Fellow · 📊~220,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Andreas Krause](https://las.inf.ethz.ch/krausea)** — ETH Zürich (Switzerland; origin: Germany) — Bayesian optimization, active learning, Gaussian process, secure reinforcement learning; Submodular optimization, Bayesian optimization, Gaussian process bandit (GP-UCB), secure search 🏆ACM Fellow, ELLIS Fellow, NSF CAREER, Test-of-Time賞 · 📊60,000+ citations / h-index 80+ (approx.)
- **[Andrew Ng](https://www.andrewng.org/)** — Stanford University / DeepLearning.AI / Coursera (USA; origin: UK/Singapore) — Deep learning, large-scale education (MOOC), reinforcement learning (helicopter control); Co-founder of Google Brain, head of Baidu AI. Popularizing machine learning education by co-founding Coursera. Inverse reinforcement learning/autonomous helicopter control. 🏆Time 100, IEEE等講演多数 · 📊approx. 250,000+
- **[Anima Anandkumar](https://www.eas.caltech.edu/people/anima)** — California Institute of Technology / NVIDIA (former) (USA; origin: India) — Tensor method, non-convex optimization, neural operator (scientific AI); Theory of latent variable model learning using tensor decomposition. Scientific calculation AI using Fourier Neural Operator. 🏆IEEE Kiyo Tomiyasu Award, Sloan Fellowship, AAAI/NSF CAREER · 📊approx. 50,000+
- **[Ashish Vaswani](https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=oR9sCGYAAAAJ)** — Essential AI (共同創業) (USA; origin: India) — Transformer, self-attention mechanism, sequence modeling; Lead author of "Attention Is All You Need" (2017) and main designer of Transformer architecture. It laid the foundation for modern large-scale language models. 🏆NeurIPS Test of Time候補級の影響 · 📊approx. 170,000+ (main paper)
- **[Been Kim](https://beenkim.github.io/)** — Google DeepMind (USA; origin: South Korea) — Interpretability, Concept Activation Vector (TCAV), Explainable AI; Established concept-based interpretability methods such as TCAV (Testing with Concept Activation Vectors). Fundamental research on explainable AI. 🏆NeurIPS/ICML被引用上位, 招待講演多数 · 📊approx. 30,000+
- **[Bernhard Schölkopf](https://www.is.mpg.de/~bs)** — Max Planck Institute for Intelligent Systems (Germany) — Kernel method, causal inference, learning theory; Development of kernel method/SVM, kernel PCA, bridging causal inference and machine learning 🏆ACM Fellow, Leibniz Prize 2018, BBVA Frontiers of Knowledge Award · 📊300,000+ citations / h-index 150+ (approx.)
- **[Bo Han](https://bhanml.github.io/)** — Hong Kong Baptist University / RIKEN AIP (Hong Kong; origin: China) — Reliable machine learning, noise label learning, robust learning; Learning under noise labels (co-teaching), reliable machine learning, robust learning theory 🏆RGC Early Career Award, MIT TR35 Asia Pacific, 高被引用研究者 · 📊20,000+ citations / h-index 50+ (approx.)
- **[Chelsea Finn](https://ai.stanford.edu/~cbfinn/)** — Stanford University / Physical Intelligence (United States) — Meta learning, robot learning, deep reinforcement learning; MAML (model-independent meta-learning), vision-based robot learning, robot-based model 🏆Sloan Fellow, MIT TR35, ACM Doctoral Dissertation Award Honorable Mention · 📊50,000+ citations / h-index 60+ (approx.)
- **[Cho-Jui Hsieh](https://web.cs.ucla.edu/~chohsieh/)** — UCLA / Google (United States; origin: Taiwan) — Large-scale optimization, adversarial robustness, LLM efficiency; Coordinate descent, large-scale optimization, adversarial robustness, neural network verification 🏆NSF CAREER, 高被引用研究者 · 📊40,000+ citations / h-index 70+ (approx.)
- **[Christopher Ré](https://cs.stanford.edu/~chrismre/)** — Stanford University (USA) — Weakly supervised learning (Snorkel), data-centric AI, efficient ML, FlashAttention; Co-proponent of Snorkel (weakly supervised learning), Data-centric AI, Hogwild!, and FlashAttention/S4. Leading the bridge between database and ML. 🏆MacArthur Fellowship (2015), ACM Fellow, SIGMOD/PODS最優秀論文 · 📊approx. 50,000+
- **[Corinna Cortes](https://research.google/people/corinnacortes/)** — Google Research (USA; origin: Denmark) — Support Vector Machine (SVM), Learning Theory, Large-Scale Machine Learning; Original author of Support Vector Network (SVM, co-authored with Vapnik). Research on learning theory, kernel methods, and large-scale learning. Vice President of Google Research. 🏆ACM Paris Kanellakis Award (2008), AAAI Fellow · 📊approx. 80,000+
- **[Cynthia Rudin](https://users.cs.duke.edu/~cynthia/)** — Duke University (USA) — Interpretable machine learning, AI for high-risk areas, optimal decision trees/scoring; Fundamental research on interpretable machine learning. Bringing inherently interpretable models to high-risk areas rather than black boxes. 🏆AAAI Squirrel AI Award (2022), INFORMS等多数, AAAI Fellow · 📊approx. 40,000+
- **[Dacheng Tao](https://www.ntu.edu.sg/)** — Nanyang Technological University (元University of Sydney) (Singapore; origin: China) — Representation learning, computer vision, deep learning theory; Multi-view learning, representation learning, deep learning optimization/generalization, large-scale vision learning 🏆IEEE/ACM Fellow, AAAS Fellow, Australian Laureate Fellow, 高被引用研究者 · 📊100,000+ citations / h-index 150+ (approx.)
- **[David Duvenaud](https://www.cs.toronto.edu/~duvenaud/)** — University of Toronto (Canada) — Neural ODE, approximate inference, regularization flow, differentiable learning; Established the foundations of differentiable models, including the proposal of neural ordinary differential equations (Neural ODE), continuous normalized flow, and molecular fingerprinting by graph convolution. 🏆NeurIPS Best Paper (Neural ODEs) · 📊~32,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[David Silver](https://www.davidsilver.uk/)** — Google DeepMind / University College London (United Kingdom) — Deep reinforcement learning, game AI, self-competitive learning; AlphaGo, AlphaZero, MuZero, DQN basics, establishment of deep reinforcement learning 🏆ACM Prize in Computing 2019, Royal Academy of Engineering Fellow · 📊250,000+ citations / h-index 70+ (approx.)
- **[Diederik P. Kingma](https://dpkingma.com/)** — Anthropic (United States; origin: Netherlands) — Variational autoencoder (VAE), variational inference, regularization flow, stochastic optimization; Proposed variational autoencoder (VAE) and Auto-Encoding Variational Bayes, developed Adam optimizer, normalized flow Glow, and variational diffusion model. 🏆ICLR Test of Time Award · 📊~370,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Dmitry Vetrov](https://www.hse.ru/en/staff/dvetrov/)** — Constructor University Bremen (元HSE/Skoltech, ロシア) (Germany; origin: Russia) — Bayesian deep learning, Bayesian inference, graphical model, deep learning; Build Russia's strongest ML group (Bayesian method). Research on Bayesian deep learning and variational inference. Winner of Yandex ML Prize Hall of Fame. 🏆Yandex ML Prize (Hall of Fame), Elsevier Research Excellence Award Russia · 📊13,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Doina Precup](https://www.cs.mcgill.ca/~dprecup/)** — McGill University / Mila / Google DeepMind (Canada; origin: Romania) — Reinforcement learning, temporal abstraction (options), AI for good; options framework (temporal abstraction), off-policy learning, reinforcement learning theory 🏆CIFAR AI Chair, Canada Research Chair, AAAI/ACM Fellow · 📊30,000+ citations / h-index 50+ (approx.)
- **[Elias Bareinboim](https://causalai.net/)** — Columbia University (United States; origin: Brazil) — Causal inference, causal AI, counterfactual inference, causality and reinforcement learning; Build theories on the transportability of causal effects, data integration, and the fusion of causality and reinforcement learning. Leading causal AI research. 🏆NSF CAREER Award, AAAI/IJCAI awards · 📊~10,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Finale Doshi-Velez](https://finale.seas.harvard.edu/)** — Harvard University (USA) — Interpretability, probabilistic models, medical AI, reinforcement learning; Proposing an evaluation framework for interpretable machine learning. Research on probabilistic models and offline reinforcement learning for medical applications. 🏆Sloan Fellowship, AAAI/NSF CAREER · 📊approx. 20,000+
- **[Francis Bach](https://www.di.ens.fr/~fbach/)** — INRIA / École Normale Supérieure (PSL) (France) — Convex optimization, kernel method, stochastic optimization, sparse learning; Stochastic optimization (SAG), sparse method, theory of kernel method, systemization of optimization 🏆ERC Grant, Lagrange Prize, IEEE/ACM論文多数 · 📊100,000+ citations / h-index 90+ (approx.)
- **[Hao Zhang](https://haozhang.ai/)** — UC San Diego (Hao AI Lab) (United States; origin: China) — ML system, LLM serving (vLLM/DistServe), LLM evaluation (Chatbot Arena), Vicuna, distributed learning (Alpa); Co-founder of LMSYS. Leads Vicuna, Chatbot Arena (LMArena), vLLM, DistServe, and Alpa. Leads LLM serving and human evaluation infrastructure. 🏆Sloan Research Fellow (2026), OSDI Best Paper Award (2021), Google ML and Systems Award (2025) · 📊~32,000 citations (Google Scholar)
- **[Hugo Jair Escalante](https://ccc.inaoep.mx/~hugojair/)** — INAOE (Instituto Nacional de Astrofísica, Óptica y Electrónica) (Mexico) — AutoML, Meta Learning, Machine Learning Challenge Design, Vision & Language; He led ChaLearn's ML/AutoML challenge for many years and established evaluation standards for meta learning and automatic machine learning. Represents AI research in Mexico. 🏆Mexican System of Researchers Fellow · 📊9800 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Ian Goodfellow](https://www.iangoodfellow.com/)** — Google DeepMind (元Apple) (United States) — Generative Adversarial Network (GAN), Adversarial Examples, Deep Learning; Invention of GAN, research on adversarial cases, co-author of textbook "Deep Learning" 🏆MIT TR35, NeurIPS高引用論文 · 📊400,000+ citations / h-index 60+ (approx.)
- **[Ilya Sutskever](https://www.cs.toronto.edu/~ilya/)** — Safe Superintelligence Inc. (元OpenAI) (United States; origin: Russia / Israel / Canada) — Deep learning, sequence learning, large-scale language models; Fundamentals of AlexNet, Seq2Seq, large-scale language model promotion, and GPT series 🏆MIT TR35, 高被引用研究者 · 📊600,000+ citations / h-index 70+ (approx.)
- **[J. Zico Kolter](http://zicokolter.com/)** — Carnegie Mellon University (United States) — Adversarial robustness, differentiability of convex optimization, deep equilibrium models, reliable learning; Proposed adversarial robustness (convex relaxation/randomized smoothing), optimization layer (OptNet), and deep equilibrium model. Leading robust and reliable learning. 🏆Sloan Fellowship · 📊~25,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Jacob Steinhardt](https://jsteinhardt.stat.berkeley.edu/)** — UC Berkeley (United States) — AI alignment, model evaluation/measurement, robustness, interpretability, reward hacking; Leading ML robustness, reward specification, scalable alignment, and prediction and measurement of emergent behavior. Also contributed to MMLU etc. AI2050 Early Career Fellow. 🏆AI2050 Early Career Fellow (Schmidt Sciences) · 📊~49,000 citations (Google Scholar)
- **[James T. Kwok](https://www.cse.ust.hk/~jamesk/)** — Hong Kong University of Science and Technology (China) — Kernel method, meta-learning, optimization, deep learning; Major achievements over many years in kernel methods, meta-learning, and large-scale optimization. IEEE Fellow. 🏆IEEE Fellow · 📊highly cited(approx., Google Scholar)
- **[Jeff Dean](https://research.google/people/jeff/)** — Google DeepMind (Chief Scientist) (USA) — Large-scale distributed systems, MapReduce/TensorFlow, deep learning infrastructure; Build large-scale ML/system infrastructure such as MapReduce, BigTable, TensorFlow, TPU, DistBelief, word2vec (jointly). 🏆ACM Fellow, ACM-IEEE Eckert-Mauchly Award, National Academy of Engineering · 📊approx. 300,000+
- **[Jian Tang](https://jian-tang.com/)** — Mila / HEC Montréal (Canada; origin: China) — Graph representation learning, AI drug discovery, representation learning; LINE (network embedding), graph representation learning, AI drug discovery (TorchDrug) 🏆CIFAR AI Chair, AAAI論文多数、高被引用研究者 · 📊30,000+ citations / h-index 50+ (approx.)
- **[Jimmy Ba](https://jimmylba.github.io/)** — University of Toronto / Vector Institute (Canada) — Optimization algorithm, deep learning, attention mechanism, Layer Normalization; Creator of the Adam optimization algorithm (co-authored with Kingma). He is also the proponent of layer normalization and laid the foundation for the standard learning method for deep learning. 🏆Sloan Research Fellowship · 📊320,000 citations
- **[Jinwoo Shin](https://alinlab.kaist.ac.kr/shin.html)** — KAIST (South Korea) — Deep learning theory, self-supervised learning, reinforcement learning, efficient learning; Numerous top conference results in self-supervised learning, out-of-distribution detection, and efficient deep learning. Leading KAIST's ML. 🏆KAIST ICT Endowed Chair · 📊highly cited(approx., Google Scholar)
- **[Joan Bruna](https://cims.nyu.edu/~bruna/)** — New York University (Courant) (USA; origin: Spain) — Geometric deep learning, graph neural network, mathematics of deep learning; Early proponent of spectral graph convolutional nets. Researches the mathematical foundations of scattering transformations, geometric deep learning, and deep nets. 🏆Sloan Fellowship, NSF CAREER · 📊approx. 30,000+
- **[John Jumper](https://deepmind.google/)** — Google DeepMind (UK; origin: USA) — Protein structure prediction, AlphaFold, deep learning application to computational biology; Technical lead for AlphaFold2. We have developed a deep learning system that predicts protein 3D structures with high accuracy from amino acid sequences, revolutionizing structural biology. 🏆Nobel Prize in Chemistry (2024), Lasker Award (2023), Breakthrough Prize · 📊approx. 60,000+
- **[Joseph E. Gonzalez](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~jegonzal/)** — UC Berkeley (USA) — ML system, graph parallel computing (GraphLab), efficient inference serving; Fundamental research on LLM systems such as graph parallel ML using GraphLab/PowerGraph, Clipper/model serving, vLLM and Chatbot Arena. 🏆MLSys等被引用上位 · 📊approx. 40,000+
- **[Jun Zhu](https://ml.cs.tsinghua.edu.cn/~jun/)** — Tsinghua University (China) — Bayesian deep learning, deep generative models, probabilistic machine learning; A world-renowned researcher in Bayesian machine learning and deep generative models (including diffusion models). Also developed such as ZhuSuan. 🏆ACM Fellow, IEEE Fellow, AAAI Fellow · 📊~67,000 citations (approx., Google Scholar)
- **[Kamalika Chaudhuri](https://cseweb.ucsd.edu/~kamalika/)** — UC San Diego / Meta AI (FAIR) (United States; origin: India) — Differential privacy, robustness, reliable machine learning, statistical learning theory; Establishing a theoretical basis for differentially private empirical risk minimization. Elucidating the relationship between privacy and robust statistics. Leading with reliable ML theory. 🏆NSF CAREER Award · 📊~20,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Kyunghyun Cho](https://kyunghyuncho.me/)** — New York University / Genentech (United States; origin: South Korea) — Deep learning, sequence model, machine translation, natural language processing; GRU, neural machine translation with attention mechanism, basics of encoder/decoder 🏆Samsung Ho-Am Prize, NAVER/Google Faculty Award · 📊200,000+ citations / h-index 80+ (approx.)
- **[Le Song](https://dasongle.github.io/)** — MBZUAI / GenBio AI (United Arab Emirates; origin: China) — Kernel embedding, graphical model, structured prediction, graph learning; Led the Hilbert space embedding of distributions (kernel mean embedding), kernel methods for graphical models, and learning of structured data. 🏆NSF CAREER Award, Best Paper Awards (NeurIPS/ICML/AISTATS) · 📊~40,000 citations; source: Google Scholar 2026
- **[Léon Bottou](https://leon.bottou.org/)** — Meta (FAIR) (United States; origin: France) — Stochastic gradient descent, large-scale learning, causal inference; Theory of large-scale stochastic gradient descent, practical application of SGD, causal inference and machine learning, DjVu 🏆ICML Test of Time Award 2018, AAAI/ACM論文多数 · 📊150,000+ citations / h-index 70+ (approx.)
- **[Masashi Sugiyama](https://www.ms.k.u-tokyo.ac.jp/sugi/)** — RIKEN AIP / University of Tokyo (Japan) — Weakly supervised learning, density ratio estimation, robust learning, machine learning theory; Theory of density ratio estimation, covariate shift adaptation, weakly supervised learning (noisy label, PU learning) 🏆Japan Academy Medal, JSPS Prize, IEEE/AAAI関連受賞 · 📊50,000+ citations / h-index 80+ (approx.)
- **[Max Welling](https://staff.fnwi.uva.nl/m.welling/)** — University of Amsterdam / CuspAI (元Microsoft) (Netherlands) — Bayesian deep learning, variational autoencoder, graph neural network, equivariant; Variational autoencoder (VAE), graph convolutional net (GCN), stochastic gradient Langevin, equivariant neural network 🏆ELLIS Fellow, ECCV/ICML論文多数 · 📊150,000+ citations / h-index 90+ (approx.)
- **[Michael Bronstein](https://www.cs.ox.ac.uk/people/michael.bronstein/)** — University of Oxford (UK; origin: Israel) — Geometric deep learning, graph neural network, 3D shape analysis; Proposed the term "geometric deep learning" and systematized deep learning for non-Euclidean data. Representative researcher of 3D shape analysis and GNN. 🏆ERC Grants, IEEE Fellow, Royal Society Wolfson Fellow · 📊approx. 60,000+
- **[Min-Ling Zhang](http://palm.seu.edu.cn/zhangml/)** — Southeast University (China) — Multi-label learning, unlabeled learning, weakly supervised learning; Representative researcher of multi-label learning. Leading the field with ML-kNN and numerous surveys. 🏆AAAI/IEEE/IAPR Fellow · 📊highly cited(approx., Google Scholar)
- **[Percy Liang](https://cs.stanford.edu/~pliang/)** — Stanford University (United States) — Foundation model, reliable machine learning, robustness; Fundamental model research (CRFM), distribution shift robustness, influence function, evaluation benchmark 🏆Presidential Early Career Award (PECASE), Sloan Fellow, IJCAI Computers and Thought Award · 📊70,000+ citations / h-index 70+ (approx.)
- **[Pieter Abbeel](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~pabbeel/)** — UC Berkeley / Covariant (United States; origin: Belgium) — Reinforcement learning, robot learning, imitation learning; Contribution to deep reinforcement learning, imitation learning, robot operation learning, TRPO/meta-learning 🏆ACM Prize候補級, IEEE Fellow, NSF CAREER · 📊150,000+ citations / h-index 100+ (approx.)
- **[Quoc V. Le](https://research.google/people/quocle/)** — Google DeepMind (USA; origin: Vietnam) — Sequence transformation (seq2seq), neural architecture exploration (AutoML), self-supervised learning; Joint proposal of seq2seq, origin of AutoML/neural architecture exploration, doc2vec, fundamental research on semi-supervised learning. 🏆NeurIPS/ICML被引用上位 · 📊approx. 180,000+
- **[Rich Caruana](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/people/rcaruana/)** — Microsoft Research (USA) — Multi-task learning, ensemble/distillation, interpretable models (GAM); Fundamental paper on multi-task learning. Ensemble selection/model compression (a precursor to distillation). Interpretable generalized additive models (EBM). 🏆KDD test-of-time等 · 📊approx. 50,000+
- **[Richard S. Sutton](http://incompleteideas.net/)** — University of Alberta / Keen Technologies (元DeepMind) (Canada; origin: United States) — Reinforcement learning, temporal difference learning, policy gradient; Systematization of reinforcement learning, TD learning, textbook "Reinforcement Learning: An Introduction" 🏆Turing Award 2024 (Bartoと共同), Royal Society Fellow · 📊150,000+ citations / h-index 80+ (approx.)
- **[Ruslan Salakhutdinov](https://www.cs.cmu.edu/~rsalakhu/)** — Carnegie Mellon University (USA; origin: Russia) — Deep Boltzmann machine, deep generative model, representation learning; Deep Boltzmann machine, dimensionality reduction using autoencoders (co-authored with Hinton), pioneer of deep generative models. Former AI research director at Apple. 🏆Sloan Fellowship, NSF CAREER, Canada Research Chair · 📊approx. 270,000+
- **[Rémi Lam](https://www.linkedin.com/in/remi-lam/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: France) — AI×weather forecasting, GraphCast, graph neural network, medium-term global forecasting, Earth system modeling; Lead researcher of GraphCast (medium-term global weather forecast using GNN). Achieved accuracy and speed exceeding ECMWF and published in Science magazine. 🏆Nature's 10 (2024) · 📊~6,000 citations (Google Scholar)
- **[Sergey Levine](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~svlevine/)** — UC Berkeley / Google DeepMind / Physical Intelligence (United States; origin: Russia / United States) — Deep reinforcement learning, robot learning, offline reinforcement learning; Deep reinforcement learning (SAC, GPS), offline RL, robot-based model 🏆NSF CAREER, 高被引用研究者 · 📊150,000+ citations / h-index 100+ (approx.)

## 📐 Learning Theory (COLT / ALT / AISTATS)

## 🧮 Theoretical Computer Science (FOCS / STOC / SODA / ICALP / STACS / ESA)

- **[Aleksander Mądry](https://people.csail.mit.edu/madry/)** — MIT (USA; origin: Poland) — Fast graph algorithms, maximum flow, continuous optimization, machine learning robustness, optimization; High-speed algorithm of maximum flow/minimum cost flow (groundbreaking speedup using electric flow/interior point method), and in recent years has led the theory of robustness and adversarial examples of machine learning models. 🏆FOCS Best Paper, Sloan Research Fellowship, Presburger Award候補級 · 📊~20,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Alexander A. Razborov](https://people.cs.uchicago.edu/~razborov/)** — University of Chicago / Steklov Mathematical Institute (USA/Russia; origin: Russia) — Computational complexity, circuit lower bound, proof complexity, communication complexity, combinatorics; Fundamental contributions in hyperpolynomial lower bounds of monotone circuits, wall theory of natural proofs (co-authored with Rudich), proof complexity and communication complexity. 🏆Nevanlinna Prize (1990), Gödel Prize (2007), Erdős Lecturer · 📊~15,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Andrew Chi-Chih Yao](https://iiis.tsinghua.edu.cn/yao/)** — Tsinghua University (清華大学) (China; origin: China/Taiwan) — Computational complexity, communication complexity, pseudorandom number generation, cryptography, quantum computing; Established the theory of communication complexity and pioneered Yao's minimax principle, the computational basis of pseudorandom number generation, quantum circuit complexity, etc. Established a world-class TCS research center (IIIS) in China. 🏆Turing Award (2000), Knuth Prize (1996), Kyoto Prize · 📊~40,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Ankur Moitra](https://people.csail.mit.edu/moitra/)** — MIT (USA; origin: India) — Algorithmic machine learning, robust statistics, tensor decomposition, optimization, computational complexity; He is a leader in rigorous algorithm theory for machine learning, including efficient algorithms for high-dimensional robust statistics, learning of Gaussian mixture distributions, non-negative matrix factorization and tensor methods. 🏆Gödel Prize (2026), Sloan Research Fellowship, Packard Fellowship · 📊~12,000+ citations (approx.)

Karlin](https://homes.cs.washington.edu/~karlin/)** — University of Washington (USA) — Online algorithms, randomization algorithms, algorithmic game theory, approximation algorithms, TSP; Fundamentals of online algorithms and competitive analysis, randomization algorithms, and recent breakthroughs in improving the approximation ratio of symmetric TSP to less than 3/2 (co-authored with Klein and Oveis Gharan). 🏆FOCS Best Paper (2020), ACM Fellow, AAAS Fellow · 📊~15,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Avi Wigderson](https://www.math.ias.edu/avi)** — Institute for Advanced Study (Princeton) (USA; origin: Israel) — Computational complexity theory, randomness and pseudorandom numbers, derandomization, zero-knowledge proofs, combinatorics; Redefining the role of randomness in calculations. His fundamental research on Nisan-Wigderson's pseudo-random number generator, the trade-off between hardness and randomness (results in the direction of P=BPP), and zero-knowledge proofs had a great impact on computational complexity. 🏆Turing Award (2023), Abel Prize (2021), Nevanlinna Prize (1994), Knuth Prize (2019), Gödel Prize (2009) · 📊~60,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Boaz Barak](https://www.boazbarak.org/)** — Harvard University / OpenAI (USA; origin: Israel) — Computational complexity, cryptography theory, Sum-of-Squares, deep learning theory; A leading figure in computational complexity and cryptography. - **[Christos H. Papadimitriou](https://www.engineering.columbia.edu/faculty/christos-papadimitriou)** — Columbia University (USA; origin: Greece) — Computational complexity, algorithmic game theory, optimization, fusion of computation with economics and biology; We defined the complexity class PPAD and created a framework for studying the difficulty of Nash equilibrium calculations. Leading the way in organizing combinatorial optimization/algorithms into textbooks and integrating calculations with other fields (economy, biology, brain). 🏆Knuth Prize (2002), Gödel Prize (2012), EATCS Award, IEEE John von Neumann Medal · 📊~80,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Constantinos Daskalakis](https://people.csail.mit.edu/costis/)** — MIT (USA; origin: Greece) — Algorithmic game theory, Nash equilibrium complexity, auction design, machine learning theory, learning probability distributions; Prove that Nash equilibrium calculation is PPAD complete. Exploring the boundaries between TCS, economics, and machine learning, including analysis of the complexity of multi-item auctions, distribution learning, and EM algorithms. 🏆Nevanlinna Prize (2018), Gödel Prize (2008), Grace Murray Hopper Award (2018) · 📊~20,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Cynthia Dwork](https://dwork.seas.harvard.edu/)** — Harvard University (USA) — Differential privacy, cryptography, distributed computing, algorithmic fairness, computational complexity; Introducing and developing differential privacy to make data privacy a science. - **[Peter W. Shor](https://math.mit.edu/~shor/)** — MIT (USA) — Quantum computing, quantum algorithms, quantum error correction, quantum information theory, combinatorial optimization; Discovered Shor's algorithm for solving prime factorization of integers and discrete logarithms in polynomial time. He also proposed quantum error-correcting codes, laying the theoretical foundation for the feasibility of quantum computing. 🏆Nevanlinna Prize (1998), Gödel Prize (1999), Dirac Medal, Breakthrough Prize in Fundamental Physics (2023) · 📊~60,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Pinyan Lu](http://itcs.sufe.edu.cn/~lupinyan/)** — Shanghai University of Finance and Economics (China) — Algorithmic game theory, computational complexity, mechanism design, approximation algorithms, optimization; Research on dichotomy and holant problems, algorithmic game theory and mechanism design. Leading TCS research in China. 🏆CCF优秀博士論文関連, ICCM Best Paper · 📊~4,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Ran Raz](https://www.cs.princeton.edu/~ranr/)** — Princeton University (USA; origin: Israel) — Computational complexity, communication complexity, proof complexity, quantum complexity, circuit lower bound; Fundamental contributions in the parallel repetition theorem, lower bounds on communication complexity and branching programs, trade-offs between memory and learning, and lower bounds on quantum information. 🏆FOCS/STOC Best Paper複数, Israel Mathematical Union関連 · 📊~10,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Richard M. Karp](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~karp/)** — UC Berkeley (USA) — NP completeness, combinatorial optimization, randomization algorithm, computational biology, online algorithm; Presented 21 NP-complete problems and established a framework for computational difficulty research. Contributed to numerous algorithms such as Edmonds-Karp, Hopcroft-Karp, and Rabin-Karp, and to the foundations of randomization and parallel computing. 🏆Turing Award (1985), Kyoto Prize, Knuth Prize (1996年第1回受賞者では無いが受賞) · 📊~70,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Robert E. Tarjan](https://www.cs.princeton.edu/people/profile/ret)** — Princeton University (USA) — Graph algorithms, data structures, balanced search trees, network flows, amortized analysis; Constructed many basic algorithms and data structures, such as depth-first search-based graph algorithms (strongly connected components and planarity determination), splay trees, Fibonacci heaps, and union-find analysis. 🏆Turing Award (1986), Nevanlinna Prize (1982) · 📊~120,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Ryan Williams](https://people.csail.mit.edu/rrw/)** — MIT (USA) — Computational complexity, circuit lower bound, fine-grained complexity, algorithm design, SAT; Contributed to the development of fine-grained complexity by proving the circuit lower bound NEXP⊄ACC0 using an algorithmic method (a program that derives the lower bound from an algorithm). 🏆Gödel Prize候補級の業績, Alan T. Waterman Award候補級, Presburger Award (2017, Vassilevskaと別) · 📊~8,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Scott Aaronson](https://scottaaronson.blog/)** — University of Texas at Austin (USA) — Quantum complexity, quantum complexity, quantum supremacy, computational complexity, theory of AI safety; He is a leader in quantum complexity through his research on quantum complexity theory (BQP and polynomial hierarchies, Boson Sampling, and the theoretical foundations of quantum supremacy), quantum testimony, and the learnability of quantum states. 🏆Tomassoni-Chisesi Prize, ACM Prize in Computing (2020), Vannevar Bush Faculty Fellowship · 📊~20,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Shafi Goldwasser](https://people.csail.mit.edu/shafi/)** — UC Berkeley / MIT / Weizmann Institute (USA; origin: USA/Israel) — Cryptography, probabilistic cryptography, zero-knowledge proofs, interactive proofs, computational complexity, property testing; Established the basis of interactive proofs leading to probabilistic cryptography, semantic security, zero-knowledge interactive proofs, and probabilistic verifiable proofs (PCP), and made modern cryptography a science. 🏆Turing Award (2012), Gödel Prize (1993, 2001), Knuth Prize (2025), RSA Award · 📊~90,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Silvio Micali](https://people.csail.mit.edu/silvio/)** — MIT (USA; origin: Italy) — Cryptography, zero-knowledge proofs, secure multiparty computation, pseudorandom numbers, blockchain theory; Together we will build the theoretical foundations of modern cryptography, including probabilistic cryptography, zero-knowledge interactive proofs, verifiable random functions, and secure computational protocols. 🏆Turing Award (2012), Gödel Prize (1993), RSA Award · 📊~80,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Subhash Khot](https://cs.nyu.edu/~khot/)** — New York University (Courant Institute) (USA; origin: India) — Computational complexity, difficulty of approximation, Unique Games Conjecture, probabilistic verifiable proof, discrete analysis; He proposed the Unique Games Conjecture, which enabled a unified explanation of the difficulty of approximation of many optimization problems. It produced one of the most studied conjectures in theoretical computer science. 🏆Nevanlinna Prize (2014), Gödel Prize (2025), MacArthur Fellowship, Alan T. Waterman Award · 📊~20,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Takeshi Tokuyama](https://dblp.org/pid/t/TakeshiTokuyama.html)** — Kwansei Gakuin University / Tohoku University (名誉教授) (Japan) — Computational geometry, combinatorial optimization, algorithms, discrete geometry, data structures; Research on computational geometry and combinatorial optimization algorithms, k-level complexity, and geometric optimization. Leading the Japanese computational geometry/discrete algorithm community. 🏆IEICE業績賞, ACM Fellow関連業績 · 📊~3,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Tim Roughgarden](https://timroughgarden.org/)** — Columbia University (USA) — Algorithmic game theory, price disorder, mechanism design, approximation algorithm, blockchain theory; He is a leading figure in the analysis of price anarchy, its robustness, mechanism design, and the theory of blockchain transaction fee mechanisms in recent years. 🏆Gödel Prize (2012), Grace Murray Hopper Award (2009), Kalai Prize · 📊~30,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Umesh Vazirani](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~vazirani/)** — UC Berkeley (USA; origin: India) — Quantum computing, quantum complexity, quantum verification, algorithms, computational complexity; Co-founded quantum complexity theory. Build the theoretical foundations of the Bernstein-Vazirani algorithm, quantum Fourier transform, and quantum device verification (quantum supremacy verification, etc.). 🏆Fulkerson Prize関連業績, ACM Fellow · 📊~30,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Venkatesan Guruswami](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~venkatg/)** — UC Berkeley (USA; origin: India) — Coding theory, list decoding, computational complexity, difficulty of approximation, pseudorandom numbers; Fundamental contributions in coding theory and TCS, including list decoding of algebraic-geometric codes with Sudan, codes reaching capacity, and the bisection theorem for approximation difficulty/constraint satisfaction problems (CSP). 🏆Gödel Prize (2012), Presburger Award (2012), Guggenheim Fellowship · 📊~15,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Virginia Vassilevska Williams](https://people.csail.mit.edu/virgi/)** — MIT (USA; origin: Bulgaria) — Algorithm design, matrix multiplication, fine-grained complexity, graph algorithms, dynamic algorithms; A series of results that improved the exponent of fast matrix multiplication, established fine-grained complexity (conditional lower bounds based on SETH, etc.), and had a major impact on shortest path/dynamic graph algorithms. 🏆Sloan Research Fellowship, NSF CAREER, Presburger Award候補級の業績 · 📊~10,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Xiaotie Deng](https://cfcs.pku.edu.cn/english/people/faculty/xiaotiedeng/)** — Peking University (China) — Algorithmic game theory, equilibrium calculation, online algorithm, mechanism design, combinatorial optimization; Complexity of Nash equilibrium/market equilibrium calculations, fundamentals of algorithmic game theory, research on online algorithms. Leading algorithm and game theory research in China. 🏆ACM Fellow, IEEE Fellow · 📊~12,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Éva Tardos](https://www.cs.cornell.edu/~eva/)** — Cornell University (USA; origin: Hungary) — Combinatorial optimization, network flow, algorithmic game theory, price anarchy (PoA), approximation algorithm; Fundamental contributions in strong polynomial time network flow/minimum cost flow algorithms, establishment of algorithmic game theory (analysis of price disorder), and approximation algorithms. 🏆Gödel Prize (2012), EATCS Award (2025), IEEE John von Neumann Medal (2019), Knuth Prize (2024) · 📊~40,000+ citations (approx.)

## 🕸️ Neural Networks (ICANN / IJCNN / ICONIP)

- **[Alex Graves](https://www.cs.toronto.edu/~graves/)** — Google DeepMind (UK) — Recurrent network (RNN/LSTM), CTC, neural Turing machine; Proposal of Connectionist Temporal Classification (CTC), LSTM application to handwriting/speech recognition, neural Turing machine. 🏆ICML/NeurIPS被引用上位 · 📊approx. 100,000+
- **[Byoung-Tak Zhang](https://bi.snu.ac.kr/~btzhang/)** — Seoul National University (South Korea) — Molecular computing/DNA computing learning, Bayesian evolutionary computing, cognitive robotics, developmental learning; Research on learning models based on biomolecular computation such as evolutionary learning, neural computation, and hypernetworks. Leading Korean AI research. 🏆IEEE Fellow, Korea AI Society 元会長 · 📊~20,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Christian Szegedy](https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=3QeF7mAAAAAJ)** — xAI / Google Brain (former) (USA; origin: Hungary) — Convolutional network (Inception/GoogLeNet), batch normalization, adversarial example; Fundamental contributions to deep learning such as Inception/GoogLeNet, batch normalization, and finding adversarial examples. 🏆CVPR等被引用上位 · 📊approx. 250,000+
- **[Christopher Bishop](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/people/cmbishop/)** — Microsoft Research / University of Cambridge (United Kingdom) — Neural network pattern recognition, probabilistic machine learning, Bayesian inference, mixed density networks; Author of the standard textbooks ``Neural Networks for Pattern Recognition'' and ``Pattern Recognition and Machine Learning.'' Systematizing probabilistic machine learning. 🏆Royal Academy of Engineering Fellow, Royal Society Fellow, IEEE Fellow · 📊~120,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Geoffrey Hinton](https://www.cs.toronto.edu/~hinton/)** — University of Toronto (Canada; origin: United Kingdom) — Backpropagation, Boltzmann machine, deep learning, representation learning; Popularization of error backpropagation method and establishment of basic theories of neural networks such as Boltzmann machines and deep belief networks. A central figure in the deep learning revolution. 🏆ACM A.M. Turing Award (2018), Nobel Prize in Physics (2024), IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (2005) · 📊~900,000 citations (approx.)
- **[George Em Karniadakis](https://www.brown.edu/research/projects/crunch/george-karniadakis)** — Brown University (United States; origin: Greece) — Physical Information Neural Network (PINN), Scientific Machine Learning, DeepONet, Operator Learning; Co-proponent of PINN (Physical Information Neural Network). He also pioneered operator learning such as DeepONet, creating the field of scientific machine learning. 🏆SIAM/ACM Prize in CSE, AAAS Fellow, SIAM Fellow · 📊~120,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Giacomo Indiveri](https://www.ini.uzh.ch/en/institute/people?uname=giacomo)** — Institute of Neuroinformatics, University of Zurich and ETH Zurich (Switzerland; origin: Italy) — Neuromorphic engineering, spiking neural networks, analog VLSI, brain-shaped hardware; A leading expert on neuromorphic hardware. Leads the analog VLSI implementation of spiking neurons and the design of brain-like processors. 🏆ERC Consolidator Grant · 📊~30,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[John Hopfield](https://pni.princeton.edu/john-hopfield)** — Princeton University (USA) — Hopfield network, associative memory, energy model, collective computation; He proposed an associative memory model using Hopfield networks and laid the physical foundations for neural networks. 🏆Nobel Prize in Physics (2024), IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, Dirac Medal · 📊~120,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Jürgen Schmidhuber](https://people.idsia.ch/~juergen/)** — IDSIA / KAUST (Switzerland; origin: Germany) — LSTM, recurrent neural network, meta-learning, artificial general intelligence theory; Jointly developed LSTM (long short-term memory) and laid the foundation for recurrent neural networks. Also researches meta-learning and general AI theory. 🏆IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, Helmholtz Award, IEEE CIS Award · 📊~180,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Kunihiko Fukushima](http://personalpage.flsi.or.jp/fukushima/)** — Fuzzy Logic Systems Institute (元NHK放送科学基礎研究所) (Japan) — Neocognitron, convolutional neural network, visual cortex model, self-organization; In 1979, he developed the first multilayer convolutional neural network ``Neocognitron'', creating the prototype for modern deep CNNs. 🏆Bower Award (Franklin Institute), IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, Caianiello Award · 📊~40,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Paris Perdikaris](https://directory.seas.upenn.edu/paris-perdikaris/)** — University of Pennsylvania (United States; origin: Greece) — Physical Information Neural Network (PINN), Scientific Machine Learning, Gaussian Process, Uncertainty Quantification; Co-sponsor of PINN (co-authored with Raissi, Karniadakis). Established the theory and application of deep learning that incorporates physical constraints. 🏆DARPA Young Faculty Award, U.S. DOE Early Career Award · 📊~50,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Sepp Hochreiter](https://www.jku.at/en/institute-for-machine-learning/about-us/team/sepp-hochreiter/)** — Johannes Kepler University Linz (Austria; origin: Germany) — LSTM, vanishing gradient problem, recurrent neural network; Co-inventor of Long Short-Term Memory (LSTM) (1997, co-authored with Schmidhuber). First analyze the vanishing gradient problem. We built the foundation for sequential learning. 🏆IEEE CIS Neural Networks Pioneer Award (2021) · 📊approx. 130,000+
- **[Sergey Ioffe](https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=S5zOyIkAAAAJ)** — Google (former) / industry (USA; origin: Russia) — Batch normalization, deep learning learning method, face recognition (FaceNet); Joint proposal of batch normalization greatly stabilizes deep network learning. Improvements to Inception architecture. 🏆ICML/被引用上位 · 📊approx. 150,000+
- **[Shun-ichi Amari](https://www.brain.riken.jp/en/faculty/details/49)** — RIKEN Center for Brain Science (Japan) — Information geometry, natural gradient method, learning theory, stochastic neuron; Established the mathematical foundations of neural networks and created information geometry and natural gradient methods. A pioneer in learning theory. 🏆IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, Japan Academy Prize, Caianiello Award, IEEE Fellow · 📊~80,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Stephen Grossberg](https://sites.bu.edu/steveg/)** — Boston University (USA) — Adaptive resonance theory (ART), competitive learning, cognitive neurodynamics, visual memory model; He proposed the adaptive resonance theory (ART) and laid the theoretical basis for self-organization and competitive learning. Launched Neural Networks magazine and founder of INNS. 🏆IEEE Frank Rosenblatt Award, IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, INNS創設会長 · 📊~140,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Teuvo Kohonen](https://dblp.org/pid/k/TeuvoKohonen.html)** — Aalto University (故人) (Finland) — Self-organizing map (SOM), associative memory, learning vector quantization, unsupervised learning; Invented self-organizing maps (SOM) and laid the foundation for unsupervised neural learning. A pioneer in associative memory research. 🏆IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, Frank Rosenblatt Award, IEEE Fellow · 📊~90,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Tomaso Poggio](https://poggio-lab.mit.edu/)** — MIT (USA; origin: Italy) — Computational neuroscience, learning theory, visual recognition model; One of the founders of computational neuroscience. Introducing regularization theory to computer vision. HMAX visual recognition model. Deep learning theory. 🏆AAAS Fellow, Swartz Prize, Okawa Prize, Gabor Award · 📊approx. 120,000+
- **[Yoshua Bengio](https://yoshuabengio.org/)** — Université de Montréal / Mila (Canada) — Representation learning, attention mechanism, generative model, deep learning theory, AI safety; Contributed to the theoretical foundations of deep learning and the development of representation learning, neural language models, and attention mechanisms. A central figure in the deep learning revolution. 🏆ACM A.M. Turing Award (2018), IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award, Killam Prize · 📊~900,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Dmitry Krotov](https://mitibmwatsonailab.mit.edu/people/dmitry-krotov/)** — MIT-IBM Watson AI Lab, IBM Research (United States; origin: Russia) — Modern Hopfield Net, Dense Associative Memory, associative memory, energy-based model; Proposed Dense Associative Memory (Modern Hopfield Net) with Hopfield. A theoretical bridge between associative memory and Transformer attention mechanisms. 📊~10,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Emre Neftci](https://www.neftci.net/)** — Forschungszentrum Jülich / RWTH Aachen University (Germany; origin: Switzerland) — Surrogate gradient learning, spiking neural network, neuromorphic learning, edge AI; Systematized the surrogate gradient method in SNN learning and introduced gradient-based optimization to spiking nets. 📊~14,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Razvan Pascanu](https://sites.google.com/view/razp)** — Google DeepMind; Mila (United Kingdom; origin: Romania) — Neural network optimization, continuous learning (EWC), recurrent NN, graph neural network; Analysis of RNN learning difficulty (gradient clipping), continuous learning Elastic Weight Consolidation (EWC), basic research on GNN. 📊80,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Sander M. Bohte](https://homepages.cwi.nl/~sbohte/)** — Centrum Wiskunde & Informatica (CWI) / University of Amsterdam (Netherlands) — Spiking Neural Network, SpikeProp, Energy Efficiency Learning, Computational Neuroscience; We proposed SpikeProp, an error backpropagation method for SNNs, and paved the way for supervised learning of spiking nets. Online learning FPTT is also proposed. 📊~12,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Wolfgang Maass](https://igi-web.tugraz.at/people/maass/)** — Graz University of Technology (Austria; origin: Germany) — Spiking neural networks, liquid state machines (LSM), computational neuroscience, reservoir computation; Established the computational power theory of spiking neural networks and proposed the Liquid State Machine. Laid the theoretical foundation of the third generation neural network. 📊~60,000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.

## 🤖 Artificial Intelligence (IJCAI / AAAI / ECAI / PRICAI / IAAI / KES / ILP)

- **[Adnan Darwiche](http://web.cs.ucla.edu/~darwiche/)** — University of California, Los Angeles (USA; origin: Lebanon) — Bayesian network inference, knowledge compilation, probabilistic circuits, formal foundations of explainable AI; Theoretical foundations of probabilistic inference using knowledge compilation and arithmetic circuits, and exact inference of Bayesian networks. Formal explainable AI. 🏆AAAI Fellow, ACM Fellow, AAAI Classic Paper Award · 📊~30,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Alan Bundy](https://homepages.inf.ed.ac.uk/bundy/)** — University of Edinburgh (United Kingdom) — Automatic theorem proving, inductive proof and rippling, ontology evolution, automatic construction of knowledge representation; Proposed automatic theorem proving and proof planning (rippling) for mathematical reasoning. 🏆IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (2007), Royal Society Fellow, AAAI Fellow · 📊~20,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Aravind Joshi](https://dblp.org/pid/01/2607.html)** — University of Pennsylvania (故人) (USA; origin: India) — Tree-joining grammar (TAG), computational linguistics, discourse, formal grammar theory; He proposed tree joining grammar (TAG) and laid the foundations for computational linguistics and formal grammar theory. 🏆IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (1997), ACL Lifetime Achievement Award, AAAI Fellow, Franklin Medal · 📊~45,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Armin Biere](https://cca.informatik.uni-freiburg.de/biere/)** — University of Freiburg (Germany) — SAT solver (Lingeling/Kissat), bounded model checking, hardware verification; Developed high performance SAT solvers (PicoSAT, Lingeling, Kissat) and won many SAT competitions. A pioneer of bounded model checking. 🏆CAV Award, SAT Competition 多数優勝 · 📊~30,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Barbara Grosz](https://www.eecs.harvard.edu/~grosz/)** — Harvard University (USA) — Discourse structure, cooperative planning, human-agent cooperation, dialogue theory; Laid the foundation for discourse structure theory and collaborative multi-agent planning (SharedPlans). 🏆IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (2015), AAAI Fellow, ACM Fellow, AAAI元会長 · 📊~40,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Bart Selman](https://www.cs.cornell.edu/selman/)** — Cornell University (USA; origin: Netherlands) — Satisfiability problem, local search (GSAT/WalkSAT), phase transition phenomenon, knowledge compilation; Solving SAT using stochastic local searches such as GSAT/WalkSAT, and discovering phase transition phenomena in calculation problems. Former president of AAAI. 🏆IJCAI John McCarthy Award (inaugural), AAAI Fellow, AAAS Fellow · 📊~55,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Carla Gomes](https://www.cs.cornell.edu/gomes/)** — Cornell University (USA; origin: Portugal) — Constraint inference, randomization and restart of exploration, computational sustainability, heavy tail phenomenon; Discovered the heavy tail phenomenon of combinatorial search and the randomized restart strategy. Founded the field of Computational Sustainability. 🏆AAAI Fellow, ACM Fellow, AAAS Fellow, Feigenbaum Prize · 📊~25,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Dan Roth](https://www.cis.upenn.edu/~danroth/)** — University of Pennsylvania / Oracle (USA; origin: Israel) — Learning-based reasoning, constrained conditional models, common sense reasoning, natural language understanding; Basic research on integrating learning and inference (constrained conditional models) and applying machine learning to natural language understanding. 🏆IJCAI John McCarthy Award (2017), AAAI Fellow, ACM Fellow, ACL Fellow · 📊~65,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Dana S. Nau](https://www.cs.umd.edu/~nau/)** — University of Maryland (USA) — Automatic planning, hierarchical task network (HTN), search, game tree search; Led the hierarchical task network planning (SHOP/SHOP2) and contributed to planning algorithms and search theory. Co-author of the textbook "Automated Planning". He is also known for his theory of pathology in game tree search. 🏆AAAI Fellow, ICAPS Influential Paper Award · 📊approx. 30,000+
- **[Daphne Koller](https://ai.stanford.edu/~koller/)** — insitro / Stanford University (USA; origin: Israel) — Probabilistic graphical model, Bayesian network, relational probabilistic model, computational biology; Theory and applications of probabilistic graphical models, standard textbook ``Probabilistic Graphical Models'' (co-authored with Friedman). 🏆IJCAI Computers and Thought Award (2001), ACM Prize in Computing (2008), AAAI Fellow, MacArthur Fellow · 📊~120,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Deborah McGuinness](https://www.cs.rpi.edu/~mcguinness/)** — Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute (USA) — Semantic web, ontology, descriptive logic, provenance; Significant contributions to the Semantic Web, knowledge representation and reasoning environments, and practical AI applications. Participated in OWL design. 🏆AAAI Fellow · 📊~45,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Demis Hassabis](https://deepmind.google/)** — Google DeepMind (UK) — Deep reinforcement learning, AlphaGo/AlphaZero, AlphaFold, artificial general intelligence; Co-founder and CEO of DeepMind. He led systems that defined the era, including AlphaGo, AlphaZero, and AlphaFold. Wins the 2024 Nobel Prize in Chemistry for protein structure prediction AlphaFold. 🏆Nobel Prize in Chemistry (2024), Lasker Award (2023), Breakthrough Prize, Knight Bachelor, FRS · 📊approx. 100,000+
- **[Edward Feigenbaum](https://profiles.stanford.edu/edward-feigenbaum)** — Stanford University (USA) — Expert systems, knowledge engineering, DENDRAL, MYCIN; Father of expert systems (DENDRAL, MYCIN) and knowledge engineering. Laid the foundation for knowledge-based AI. 🏆ACM A.M. Turing Award (1994), AAAI Fellow, AAAI元会長 · 📊~25,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Eugene Freuder](https://www.insight-centre.org/users/eugene-freuder/)** — University College Cork (Insight Centre) (Ireland; origin: USA) — Constraint-based inference, constraint satisfaction problem, consistency algorithm; Pioneering research on constraint-based reasoning and problem solving. Builds a foundation for consistency/search for constraint satisfaction problems. 🏆IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (2020), AAAI Fellow · 📊~20,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Francesca Rossi](https://researcher.watson.ibm.com/researcher/view.php?person=ibm-Francesca.Rossi2)** — IBM Research / University of Padova (USA; origin: Italy) — Constraint programming, soft constraints, preference inference, AI ethics and value alignment; A leader in constraint programming, soft constraint/preference theory, and AI ethics research. Former president of IJCAI and former president of AAAI. 🏆AAAI Fellow, EurAI Fellow, ACM Fellow, IJCAI元会長, AAAI元会長 · 📊~20,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Franz Baader](https://lat.inf.tu-dresden.de/~baader/)** — TU Dresden (Germany) — Descriptive logic, ontological reasoning, term rewriting, unified theory; Established the theoretical foundations of Description Logic and compiled the ``Description Logic Handbook''. The core of ontological reasoning. 🏆EurAI Fellow, Herbrand Award (2020) · 📊~45,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Hector Geffner](https://www.cs.rwth-aachen.de/~hector.geffner/)** — RWTH Aachen University / ICREA-UPF (Germany; origin: Argentina) — Domain-independent heuristic planning, model-based AI, breadth-based search, generalization planning; Establishment of domain-independent heuristic planning, breadth-based search, and integrated research on model-based and database AI. 🏆AAAI Fellow (2007), EurAI Fellow · 📊~25,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Hector Levesque](https://www.cs.toronto.edu/~hector/)** — University of Toronto (Canada) — Knowledge representation, epistemic logic, situational calculation, boundaries of accessibility, Winograd Schema; Theory of knowledge representation and inference, computability boundaries of representation and inference, situational computation and epistemic logic. Proposed Winograd Schema Challenge. 🏆IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (2013), AAAI Fellow, IJCAI Computers and Thought Award (1985) · 📊~35,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Hiroaki Kitano](https://www.oist.jp/research/hiroaki-kitano)** — Sony Computer Science Laboratories / OIST (Japan) — RoboCup, systems biology, evolutionary computation, scientific discovery by AI; Founder of RoboCup, establishment of systems biology, and advocate of scientific discovery using AI (Novel Turing Challenge). 🏆IJCAI Computers and Thought Award (1993), AAAI Fellow · 📊~60,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Ian Horrocks](https://www.cs.ox.ac.uk/people/ian.horrocks/)** — University of Oxford (United Kingdom) — Descriptive logical reasoning, OWL ontology language, tableau reasoning, ontology engineering; Highly efficient inference techniques for description logic and design of OWL ontology language. Building the foundation of the Semantic Web. 🏆Royal Society Fellow, EurAI Fellow, Semantic Web Science Association Award · 📊~60,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Joao Marques-Silva](https://jpmarquessilva.github.io/)** — ICREA / University of Lleida (Spain; origin: Portugal) — Competition-driven clause learning (CDCL), satisfiability solving, formally explainable AI, MaxSAT; The invention of competition-driven clause learning (CDCL) dramatically improved the performance of modern SAT solvers. In recent years, he has been researching formally explainable AI. 🏆CAV Award (CDCL関連), IEEE Fellow · 📊~35,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Joseph Y. Halpern](https://www.cs.cornell.edu/home/halpern/)** — Cornell University (USA; origin: Canada) — Logic of knowledge, reasoning under uncertainty, causation, multi-agent; Established the theory of Reasoning About Knowledge (co-authored with Fagin et al.), Actual Causality, and the expression of uncertainty. 🏆ACM Fellow, AAAI Fellow, IJCAI Award for Research Excellence, Gödel Prize · 📊approx. 60,000+
- **[Judea Pearl](http://bayes.cs.ucla.edu/jp_home.html)** — University of California, Los Angeles (USA; origin: Israel) — Bayesian network, causal inference, do operator, probabilistic graphical model; Established the mathematical foundations of Bayesian networks and causal inference. It revolutionized AI through probabilistic and causal reasoning. 🏆ACM A.M. Turing Award (2011), IJCAI Award for Research Excellence (1999), AAAI Fellow · 📊~190,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Katsumi Inoue](https://research.nii.ac.jp/~inoue/)** — National Institute of Informatics (NII), Japan (Japan) — Abduction reasoning, logic programming, inductive logic programming, logic applications to systems biology; Theory of hypothetical inference (abduction) and logical programming, and applications to logic-based learning and systems biology. 🏆EurAI/AAAI関連委員, 日本のAI/論理プログラミング研究を牽引 · 📊~9,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Leslie Pack Kaelbling](https://people.csail.mit.edu/lpk/)** — MIT (USA) — Planning under uncertainty (POMDP), reinforcement learning, task & motion planning, robot decision making; Planning under uncertainty such as POMDP, integration of reinforcement learning and robotics. Founding editor-in-chief of JMLR. 🏆IJCAI Computers and Thought Award (1997), AAAI Fellow, ACM Fellow · 📊~55,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Lise Getoor](https://getoor.soe.ucsc.edu/)** — University of California, Santa Cruz (USA) — Statistical relational learning, probabilistic soft logic (PSL), graph mining, knowledge discovery; Establishment of a method (Statistical Relationship Learning, PSL) that integrates probabilistic and logical representations. Graph mining and network analysis. 🏆AAAI Fellow, ACM Fellow · 📊~35,000 citations (approx.)
- **[Malik Ghallab](https://homepages.laas.fr/malik/)** — LAAS-CNRS (France) — Automatic planning and action, planning, intelligent robots; A leading figure in the field of automated planning and the main author of the standard textbooks ``Automated Planning: Theory and Practice'' and ``Automated Planning and Acting.'' Representative leader of European AI. 🏆EurAI Fellow, AAAI Fellow · 📊approx. 20,000+

## 👁️ Computer Vision (CVPR / ICCV / ECCV / BMVC / ICPR / ACCV)

- **[Abhinav Gupta](https://www.cs.cmu.edu/~abhinavg/)** — Carnegie Mellon University (USA; origin: India) — Self-supervised learning, visual representation learning, robot learning, scene understanding, large-scale learning; Leads self-supervised visual representation learning, relational networks, large-scale robot learning, and scene graph/contextual inference. 🏆PAMI Young Researcher Award, IAPR JK Aggarwal Prize · 📊~97,000 citations (Google Scholar)

- **[Alexei A. Efros](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~efros/)** — UC Berkeley (USA; origin: Russia) — Texture synthesis, image conversion (pix2pix/CycleGAN), visual data mining, self-supervised learning; Texture synthesis (image quilting), pix2pix/CycleGAN infrastructure, data-driven vision, self-supervised learning. 🏆ACM SIGGRAPH Significant New Researcher Award (2010), Helmholtz Prize, PAMI Mark Everingham Prize, Guggenheim Fellow · 📊approx. 150,000+

Leads AI2 and promotes an open model. 🏆CVPR/ICCV Best Paper関連, AI2 CEO · 📊approx. 130,000+
- **[Anderson Rocha](https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=JX1fykMAAAAJ)** — University of Campinas (UNICAMP), Institute of Computing, Recod.ai Lab (Brazil) — Digital forensics, computer vision, machine learning, media authenticity verification; A world-renowned researcher in the field of digital forensics and media authenticity verification. ## 🔊 Speech Signal Processing (InterSpeech / ICASSP)

- **[Bhuvana Ramabhadran](https://sites.google.com/view/bhuvana-ramabhadran/home)** — Google / 元IBM Research (United States; origin: India) — Speech recognition, multilingual speech processing, semi-supervised learning, speech synthesis; A leading researcher in speech recognition and multilingual speech processing for many years. He led the development of speech recognition systems at IBM and Google, and is a fellow at both ISCA and IEEE. 🏆IEEE Fellow, ISCA Fellow · 📊21,000 citations
- **[Björn W. Schuller](https://www.schuller.one/)** — Imperial College London / TU München / audEERING (UK; origin: Germany) — Emotional speech, computational paralinguistics, health estimation from speech, affective computing, speech feature extraction; Leading computational paralinguistics/emotional speech recognition, openSMILE feature extraction tool, and InterSpeech emotion/paralinguistic challenge. 🏆IEEE Fellow, ISCA Fellow, ACM Fellow · 📊60,000+ citations

## 🎮 Reinforcement Learning (NeurIPS / ICML / ICLR)

- **[Andrew G. Barto](https://people.cs.umass.edu/~barto/)** — University of Massachusetts Amherst (名誉教授) (USA) — Conceptual and algorithmic foundations of reinforcement learning, actor-critic method, temporal difference learning, reward-based decision making; Build the conceptual and algorithmic foundations of reinforcement learning. Co-authored textbook with Sutton, ``Reinforcement Learning: An Introduction,'' the origin of the actor-critic method. Winner of the Turing Award in 2024. 🏆ACM A.M. Turing Award (2024), IEEE Neural Networks Pioneer Award · 📊100,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Benjamin Recht](https://people.eecs.berkeley.edu/~brecht/)** — University of California, Berkeley (USA) — Reinforcement learning as continuous control, optimization, learning theory, LQR; Known for systematizing reinforcement learning from the perspective of continuous control, optimization theory, random features, and benchmark research on generalization. 🏆NSF CAREER · 📊78,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Benjamin Rosman](https://www.benjaminrosman.com/)** — University of the Witwatersrand (RAIL Lab) (South Africa) — Reinforcement learning, robotics, decision making, transfer learning; Co-founder of Deep Learning Indaba. Contributions in reinforcement learning and robotics. The center of building the African AI ecosystem. CIFAR Fellow. 🏆CIFAR Azrieli Global Scholar · 📊5000 citations; source: Google Scholar approx.
- **[Emma Brunskill](https://cs.stanford.edu/people/ebrun/)** — Stanford University (USA) — Offline reinforcement learning, off-policy evaluation, decision making under uncertainty, educational applications; Leading the theory and application of offline/batch RL and off-policy evaluation. - **[Jan Peters](https://www.ias.informatik.tu-darmstadt.de/Member/JanPeters)** — Technische Universität Darmstadt; DFKI (Germany) — Robot reinforcement learning, policy search, motion primitives, imitation learning; Systematic development of robot motion learning policy search (REPS, PoWER), stochastic motion primitives, and imitation learning. 🏆ERC Starting/Consolidator Grant, IEEE Fellow · 📊60,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Joelle Pineau](https://www.cs.mcgill.ca/~jpineau/)** — McGill University / Mila / Cohere (Canada) — Reinforcement learning, POMDP, reproducibility, dialogue system; Fundamental research on POMDP approximate planning (PBVI). Director of Meta FAIR. 🏆CIFAR Fellow, ACM Fellow, Royal Society of Canada · 📊approx. 40,000+

- **[Marc G. Bellemare](https://marcgbellemare.info/)** — Mila; McGill University (旧Google Brain Montréal) (Canada) — Distributed reinforcement learning, Arcade Learning Environment, risk and uncertainty, curiosity-driven exploration; Build a deep RL benchmark Arcade Learning Environment. - **[Michael Bowling](http://webdocs.cs.ualberta.ca/~bowling/)** — University of Alberta / DeepMind (Canada; origin: USA) — Reinforcement learning, incomplete information game (poker), Arcade Learning Environment; Understanding heads-up limit poker (Cepheus), DeepStack. Joint development of Arcade Learning Environment (Atari benchmark). 🏆AAAI Fellow, Science掲載複数 · 📊approx. 30,000+
- **[Oriol Vinyals](https://research.google/people/oriolvinyals/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: Spain) — Game AI (StarCraft/AlphaStar), seq2seq, point internetwork, meta-learning; Led by AlphaStar who achieved Grandmaster level in StarCraft II (published in Nature). Also jointly proposed seq2seq, Pointer Networks, and Matching Networks. 🏆MIT TR35 · 📊200,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Satinder Singh](https://web.eecs.umich.edu/~baveja/)** — University of Michigan; Google DeepMind (USA; origin: India) — Reinforcement learning theory, intrinsic motivation, multi-agent learning, decision making; Contributed to the theoretical foundations of reinforcement learning and developed intrinsic motivation RL, convergence analysis of gradient methods, etc. Co-founded the RLDM conference series. 🏆AAAI Fellow · 📊51,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Shie Mannor](https://shie.net.technion.ac.il/)** — Technion - Israel Institute of Technology; NVIDIA (Israel) — Robust Markov decision process, risk-aware RL, learning theory, stochastic optimization; Significant contributions to robust MDP, risk-aware reinforcement learning, bandits, and learning theory. 🏆IEEE Fellow · 📊38,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Shixiang Shane Gu](https://sites.google.com/view/gugurus/home)** — Google DeepMind (USA; origin: China/Japan) — Sample-efficient deep RL, Gumbel-Softmax, robot learning, LLM inference; Also contributed to the Gumbel-Softmax joint proposal, sample-efficient deep RL (NAF, Q-Prop), and Zero-shot Chain-of-Thought. 🏆Best Paper Award, CoRL 2019 · 📊30,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Stefan Schaal](https://stefan-schaal.net/)** — Intrinsic (Alphabet) (旧USC; Max Planck IS) (USA; origin: Germany) — Imitation learning, dynamic motion primitives (DMP), robot learning control, computational neuroscience; Proposed dynamic motor primitives (DMP) and established the basis for motor skill acquisition through imitation learning and reinforcement learning. Founding director of the Max Planck Institute for Intelligent Systems. 🏆IEEE Fellow · 📊50,000+ citations (approx.)

Implemented deep neural network + tree search architecture and was in charge of starting the match against Lee Se-hyun. 📊40,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Aviral Kumar](https://aviralkumar2907.github.io/)** — Carnegie Mellon University (旧Google DeepMind/UC Berkeley) (USA; origin: India) — Offline reinforcement learning, Conservative Q-Learning (CQL), regularization of value function, LLM inference with RL; We proposed Conservative Q-Learning (CQL), a representative method for offline RL. Established conservative Q-learning that suppresses value overestimation under distribution shifts. 📊15,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Chongjie Zhang](https://engineering.washu.edu/faculty/Chongjie-Zhang.html)** — Washington University in St. Louis (旧Tsinghua University) (USA; origin: China) — Multi-agent reinforcement learning, value function decomposition, cooperation/coordination, deep RL; Proposed many theories and methods for value function decomposition of cooperative multi-agent RL (QPLEX, etc.) and deep MARL. 📊10,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Danijar Hafner](https://danijar.com/)** — Google DeepMind (USA; origin: Germany) — World model, Dreamer, behavioral learning using latent imagination, PlaNet; We proposed the Dreamer series (V1-V3) and PlaNet, which learn behavior by imagination in latent state space. DreamerV3 lets you conquer Minecraft from scratch. 📊15,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[David Abel](https://david-abel.github.io/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: USA) — Abstraction in reinforcement learning, state abstraction, fundamentals of agency, continuous learning; Systematized the theory of abstraction (state/behavior abstraction) in reinforcement learning. Exploring the fundamentals of agency, learning, and computation. 📊2,700+ citations (approx.)

He also proposes HyperNetworks, generative sketching, etc. Co-founded Sakana AI. 📊40,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[George Tucker](https://sites.google.com/view/gjt)** — Google DeepMind (USA) — Offline reinforcement learning, gradient estimator, REBAR, probabilistic model; Proposed low variance gradient estimation REBAR for discrete latent variables. - **[Hado van Hasselt](https://hadovanhasselt.com/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: Netherlands) — Double Q-learning, value estimation bias, deep reinforcement learning, general purpose agent; We proposed Double Q-learning (2010) and its deep version Double DQN (AAAI 2016) to solve the problem of overestimation of value. Leads integrated agent research such as Rainbow. 📊60,000+ citations (approx.)

Also led the development of OpenAI Gym and the development of ChatGPT by RLHF. 📊150,000+ citations (approx.)

Leading stochastic modeling and autonomous decision making. 📊20,000+ citations (approx.)

- **[Rémi Munos](https://researchers.lille.inria.fr/~munos/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: France) — Reinforcement learning theory, Monte Carlo tree search, off-policy learning, Retrace; He has made significant contributions to reinforcement learning theory, including the convergence proof of off-policy learning Retrace(λ), the theory of MCTS, and approximate dynamic programming. 📊50,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Shimon Whiteson](https://whirl.cs.ox.ac.uk/member/shimon-whiteson/)** — University of Oxford; Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: USA) — Multi-agent reinforcement learning, QMIX, value function decomposition, StarCraft Multi-Agent Challenge; Proposed QMIX (monotonic value function decomposition) and SMAC benchmarks for cooperative multi-agent RL. It also contributes to multi-agent policy gradients. 📊30,000+ citations (approx.)
- **[Tom Schaul](https://schaul.site44.com/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: Luxembourg) — Reinforcement learning, prioritized experience replay, exploration, general purpose value function; Proposed major methods of deep reinforcement learning such as Prioritized Experience Replay and Universal Value Function Approximators. Contributed to Atari/AlphaStar system research. 📊49,000 citations
- **[Tor Lattimore](https://tor-lattimore.com/)** — Google DeepMind (United Kingdom; origin: Australia) — Multi-armed bandit, linear bandit, online learning, decision making under uncertainty; Systematized the theory of bandit algorithms. How to conquer Atari like a human and published in Nature. Asynchronous method A3C is also proposed. 📊99,000+ citations (approx.)

## Contributing

Additions and corrections are welcome for researchers who meet the inclusion criteria. Edit `data/researchers.json` and run `python3 data/gen.py` (README files and notes are generated; do not edit them directly).
